CaptainCasa Demos - Documentation

This documentation contains all demos that are part of the CaptainCasa demo workplace.

The demos show how to implement dialogs using the CaptainCasa Enterprise Client framework.

A dialog is implemented by defining a layout (layout definition) as XML using a set of tags that is provided by the CaptainCasa framework. And it consists ouf of a Java class that reflectes the server side processing of this dialog.

Containers

Structuring page content

Containers to structure a dialog

This demo shows three useful container components that you may use for structuring the content of pages:

1. BOX is an empty rectangular container
2. FOLDABLEPANE is a container with a title text
3. TABBEDPANE is an arrangement of several content areas, one of them being selected

All three of them are harmonized from styling point of view.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoBoxing}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:box id="g_3" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:field id="g_6" labeltext="First name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:field id="g_9" labeltext="Last name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
</t:box>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:pane id="g_11" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_12" coldistance="10" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_13" rowalignmenty="top" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" text="Foldable" width="50%" >
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:field id="g_16" labeltext="First name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_17" >
<t:field id="g_19" labeltext="Last name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
<t:foldablepane id="g_20" rowalignmenty="top" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" text="Foldable" width="50%" >
<t:row id="g_21" >
<t:field id="g_23" labeltext="First name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>

</t:row>

<t:tabbedpane id="g_28" height="100%" width="100%" >

</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoBoxing}")

public class DemoBoxing
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    public DemoBoxing(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoboxing.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoBoxing}"; }
}

...in "exposed" style

For the components BOX, FOLDABLEPANE, TABBEDPANE there is a style variant "ccexposed" which explicitly renders some border around the components - so that they are more exposed in front of the background.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoBoxing2}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:box id="g_4" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" stylevariant="ccexposed" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:field id="g_6" labeltext="First name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>

<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:pane id="g_10" width="100%" >

<t:foldablepane id="g_12" rowalignmenty="top" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" stylevariant="ccexposed" text="Foldable" width="50%" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:field id="g_14" labeltext="First name" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_15" >

</t:row>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoBoxing2}")

public class DemoBoxing2
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    public DemoBoxing2(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoboxing2.xml"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoBoxing2}"; }

}

Panes

This page is a summary of basic pane components that are provided.

Pane components are containers that themselves can hold other components. Pane components can be nested in any way.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.demoPanes}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Pane" width="120" />
<t:pane id="g_4" background="#00000010" padding="5" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Some comment" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_7" >

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

public class DemoPanes extends PageBean
{
    int m_flashCounter = 0;

    public DemoPanes(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

    public void onFlash(ActionEvent ae)
    {
        m_flashCounter++;
    }
    
    public int getFlashCounter()
    {
        return m_flashCounter;
    }
    public void setFlashCounter(int flashCounter)
    {
        m_flashCounter = flashCounter;
    }
    
}

Foldable / Titled Pane

Basic Examples

The FOLDABLEPANE allows the user to open/close the content area by either clicking onto the FOLDABLEPANE's title text or by pressing the icon on the top right.

There are multiple ways of formatting the header line and the content area.

You can place exactly one FOLDABLEPANEHEADERROW into the FOLDABLEPANE. The content of the row is placed between the title text on the left and the toggle button on the right.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.demoFoldable}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_3" height="100" text="Initial state: opened=true" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:label id="g_5" text="Hallo" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_7" height="100" opened="false" text="Initial state: opened=false" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_9" height="100" text="Foldable with header components" width="100%" >
<t:foldablepaneheaderrow id="g_10" >
<t:icon id="g_11" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onFind}" image="/images/icons/find.png" />
<t:icon id="g_12" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onCar}" image="/images/icons/car.png" />
<t:coldistance id="g_13" />
</t:foldablepaneheaderrow>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_15" height="100" text="Foldable with image in front of text" textimage="/images/iconssvg/person_16x16.svg" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_16" />
<t:row id="g_17" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_18" foreground="#F0F0F0" headerbgpaint="rectangle(0,0,100%,100%,#680000,#FFC0C0,vertical)" height="100" text="Special coloring of header area" width="100%" >
<t:foldablepaneheaderrow id="g_19" >
<t:icon id="g_20" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onFind}" image="/images/icons/find.png" />
<t:icon id="g_21" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onCar}" image="/images/icons/car.png" />
<t:coldistance id="g_22" />
</t:foldablepaneheaderrow>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_23" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_24" enabled="false" height="100" text="Disabled folding" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_25" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_26" enabled="false" foregrounddisabled="#000080" height="100" text="Disabled folding - special text color" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_27" height="20" />
<t:row id="g_28" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_29" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onFoldableAction}" flush="true" height="100" opened="#{d.DemoFoldable.opened}" text="Server Side control of opened status" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_30" >
<t:label id="g_31" text="Opened" width="120" />
<t:checkbox id="g_32" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoFoldable.opened}" text="Opened" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_33" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_34" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_35" actionListener="#{d.demoFoldable.onFoldableAction}" flush="true" height="100" opened="true" text="FLUSH=true, an action Listener will be called" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.defaultscreens.Statusbar;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;


@CCGenClass(expressionBase="#{d.demoFoldable}")

public class DemoFoldable extends PageBean
{
    boolean m_opened = true;
    
    public DemoFoldable(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }
    
    public void setOpened(boolean value) 
    { 
        m_opened = value; 
    }
    public boolean getOpened() { return m_opened; }
    
    public void onCar(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("onCar was called!");
    }

    public void onFind(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("onFind was called!");
    }

    public void onFoldableAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("onFoldableAction was called!");
    }
}

Vertical

The component FOLABLEVERTICALPANE is a titled area that can be collapsed by the user by either pressing the text link or the icon on the left.

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

public class DemoFoldableVertical extends PageBean
{
    boolean m_leftIsOpened = true;
    boolean m_rightIsOpened = false;

    public DemoFoldableVertical(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

    public boolean getLeftIsOpened() { return m_leftIsOpened; }
    public void setLeftIsOpened(boolean leftIsOpened) { m_leftIsOpened = leftIsOpened; }

    public boolean getRightIsOpened() { return m_rightIsOpened; }
    public void setRightIsOpened(boolean rightIsOpened) { m_rightIsOpened = rightIsOpened; }

    public void onFoldableLeftAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        m_rightIsOpened = !m_leftIsOpened;
    }

    public void onFoldableRightAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        m_leftIsOpened = !m_rightIsOpened;
    }

    public void onButtonHideLeftAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        m_leftIsOpened = false;
        m_rightIsOpened = true;
    }

    public void onButtonHideRightAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        m_leftIsOpened = true;
        m_rightIsOpened = false;
    }
}

Light Style / Titled Pane

In addition to the default styling (attribute STYLEVARIANT "default") there is a second style variant "cclight" (attribute STYLEVARIANT "cclight") which comes without explicit coloring.

Please note: by setting attribute ENABLED to "false" you can switch off the dynamic behavior of the FOLDABLEPANE - and just use it as a titled area.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

Drag Drop in Title Area only

When defining DRAGSEND with a FOLDABLEPANE then by default the user can start drag operations from the whole area of the FOLDABLEPANE.

By defining attribute DRAGTITLEONLY as "true", drag activities can only be started from the title area.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoDragDropTitleOnly}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoDragDropTitleOnly}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_4" dragsend="aaa:bbb" text="Default - Drag everywhere" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Label" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_7" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_9" dragsend="aaa:bbb" dragtitleonly="true" text="Drag only in title are" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_11" text="Label" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_12" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:foldableverticalpane id="g_14" dragsend="aaa:bbb" text="Default" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_15" >
<t:label id="g_16" text="Label" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_17" width="100%;100" />
</t:row>
</t:foldableverticalpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:foldableverticalpane id="g_19" dragsend="aaa:bbb" dragtitleonly="true" text="Only TItle" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_20" >
<t:label id="g_21" text="Label" width="100" />

Additional header components

You can add additional header elements to the FOLDABLEPANE component by using its sub-component FOLDABLEPANEHEADERROW.

By default the additional elements are arranged on the right side, in front of the toggle icon. By setting attribute FOLDABLEPANE-HEADERFULLWIDTH to "true" the additional header area is defined to occupy the fully space between the title and the toggle icon - as consequence the additional components are arranged "on the left".

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoFoldablePaneHeader}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoFoldablePaneHeader}" rowdistance="20" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_2" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" text="Default - only title" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:field id="g_8" labeltext="Some content filed 1" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:field id="g_11" labeltext="Some content filed 2" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_14" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" text="Additional elements" width="100%" >
<t:foldablepaneheaderrow id="g_5" >

<t:coldistance id="g_35" width="5" />

Tab Pane

Tab Pane

The tab pane allows to set a title and an image per tab. Both attributes can be updated during runtime.

The value of the currently opened tab is transferred to the server - if defining the VALUE attribute. In addition you can set the value of attribute FLUSH to "true", then the value will be transferred immediately when the user selects a tab. - As consequence you can read in some data which is required to be displayed within the tab that the user just opened.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPane}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_3" flush="true" height="100" value="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.selectedTabIndex}" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_4" image="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.leftTabImage}" text="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.leftTabText}" />
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_5" image="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.rightTabImage}" text="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.rightTabText}" />
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_6" text="Third" />
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_7" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_9" text="Selected Index" width="120" />
<t:formattedfield id="g_10" flush="true" format="int" value="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.selectedTabIndex}" width="50" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:coldistance id="g_12" width="120" />
<t:button id="g_13" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPane.onUpdateTabTextImage}" text="Update tab text and icons" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedPane}")

public class DemoTabbedPane
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    protected int m_selectedTabIndex;
    public int getSelectedTabIndex() { return m_selectedTabIndex; }
    public void setSelectedTabIndex(int value) { m_selectedTabIndex = value; }

    public DemoTabbedPane(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

    public void onUpdateTabTextImage(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_leftTabText += "!";
        m_rightTabText += "!";
        String temp;
        temp = m_leftTabImage;
        m_leftTabImage = m_rightTabImage;
        m_rightTabImage = temp;
    }

    protected String m_rightTabText = "Right";
    public String getRightTabText() { return m_rightTabText; }
    public void setRightTabText(String value) { m_rightTabText = value; }

    protected String m_rightTabImage = "/images/icons/car.png";
    public String getRightTabImage() { return m_rightTabImage; }
    public void setRightTabImage(String value) { m_rightTabImage = value; }

    protected String m_leftTabImage = "/images/icons/disk.png";
    public String getLeftTabImage() { return m_leftTabImage; }
    public void setLeftTabImage(String value) { m_leftTabImage = value; }

    protected String m_leftTabText = "Left";
    public String getLeftTabText() { return m_leftTabText; }
    public void setLeftTabText(String value) { m_leftTabText = value; }

}

Tab Pane with close-Icon

On TABBEDPANETAB level you can define attribute WITHCLOSEICON to be "true". In this case an additional close-icon is shown within the corresponding tab.

On server side an action listener (again on TABBEDPANETAB level) is called, the event that is passed is an instance of class BaseActionEventTabClose.

In the example the closing of the tabs is done using a RENDERED attribute that is defined with each TABBEDPANE instance.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_3" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_4" clientname="TAB1" padding="10" text="This tab cannot be removed" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Some content of tab &#34;This tab cannot be removed&#34;." />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_7" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose.onLeftClose}" clientname="TABEFT" padding="10" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose.leftRendered}" text="Left Info" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_9" text="Some content of tab &#34;Left Info&#34;." />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_10" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose.onRightClose}" clientname="TABRIGHT" padding="10" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose.rightRendered}" text="Right Info" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_12" text="Some content of tab &#34;Right Info&#34;." />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:button id="g_14" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose.onShowAllTabs}" text="Show Left and Right Info Tabs" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithClose}")

public class DemoTabbedPaneWithClose
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    protected boolean m_rightRendered = true;
    protected boolean m_leftRendered = true;

    public DemoTabbedPaneWithClose(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }
    
    public boolean getRightRendered() { return m_rightRendered; }
    public boolean getLeftRendered() { return m_leftRendered; }

    public void onRightClose(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_rightRendered = false;
    }

    public void onLeftClose(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_leftRendered = false;
    }
    
    public void onShowAllTabs(ActionEvent event)
    {
        m_leftRendered = true;
        m_rightRendered = true;
    }

}

Tab Pane - Height Definition

By default and if no explicit TABPANE-HEIGHT is defined, the height of a TABPANE follows the highest height of its contained tab components.

By using attribute TABPANE-HEIGHTIFUNSELECTED you can explicitly define a height for a TABPANE if it is not selected. In the example the tabs "tab2" and "tab3" contain a quite big content - which does not influence the height of the total TABPABE component if the tabs are not selected.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneTabHeight}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_3" width="100%" onetablineonly="true" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_4" padding="10" text="tab1" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:button id="g_6" text="Some Button" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_7" heightifunselected="0" padding="10" text="tab2" >
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:button id="g_9" height="300" text="Some Button" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_10" heightifunselected="0" padding="10" text="tab3" >
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:button id="g_12" height="100" text="Some Button" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_14" text="Some content below the TABBEDPANE" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

    }

Create new tab by dummy tab

This demo shows how to use an "end-tab" with some image as kind of button to manage tabs before.

The functions used are:

1. instead of using counted indices the TABBEDPANETAB instances use a defined SELECTIONID. These selection ids are stable - if not defined, you would have to work with an counted index and would have to recalculate the index of tab permanently.
2. the TABBEDPANE is transferring the selected value directly when the user selects a tab - the FLUSH is defined to "true".
3. On server side the last tab is used to open other tabs, and to immediately move the content-value to the new tab.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:rowdistance id="g_3" height="50" />
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_5" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.onTabbedPaneAction}" flush="true" height="200" value="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.tabValue}" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_6" text="First" >
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:label id="g_8" text="Content of &#34;First&#34;" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_9" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.onTabClose2}" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.rendered2}" selectionid="SECOND" text="Second" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_11" text="Content of &#34;Second&#34;" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_12" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.onTabClose3}" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.rendered3}" selectionid="THIRD" text="Third" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:label id="g_14" text="Content of &#34;Third&#34;" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_15" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.onTabClose4}" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.rendered4}" selectionid="FOURTH" text="Fourth" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:label id="g_17" text="Content of &#34;Fourth&#34;" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_18" image="/images/iconssvg/add_16x16.svg" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.renderedPlus}" selectionid="PLUS" />
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_19" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_20" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Value of internal flags" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_21" >
<t:label id="g_22" text="Selected tab" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_23" enabled="false" text="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.tabValue}" width="100" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_24" height="5" />
<t:row id="g_25" >

</t:row>
<t:row id="g_28" >
<t:coldistance id="g_29" width="100" />
<t:checkbox id="g_30" enabled="false" selected="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.rendered3}" text="renderedThird" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_31" >
<t:coldistance id="g_32" width="100" />
<t:checkbox id="g_33" enabled="false" selected="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus.rendered4}" text="renderedForth" />
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus}")

public class DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    static final String TAB_2_SELID = "SECOND";
    static final String TAB_3_SELID = "THIRD";
    static final String TAB_4_SELID = "FOURTH";
    static final String TAB_PLUS_SELID = "PLUS";
    
    String m_tabValue;
    boolean m_rendered2 = false;
    boolean m_rendered3 = false;
    boolean m_rendered4 = false;
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demotabbedpanewithplus.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoTabbedPaneWithPlus}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public String getTabValue() { return m_tabValue; }
    public void setTabValue(String value) { this.m_tabValue = value; }

    public boolean getRendered2() { return m_rendered2; }
    public boolean getRendered3() { return m_rendered3; }
    public boolean getRendered4() { return m_rendered4; }
    public boolean getRenderedPlus() 
    { 
        return m_rendered2 == false || m_rendered3 == false || m_rendered4 == false; 
    }

    public void onTabClose2(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) { m_rendered2 = false; }
    public void onTabClose3(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) { m_rendered3 = false; }
    public void onTabClose4(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) { m_rendered4 = false; }

    public void onTabbedPaneAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (TAB_PLUS_SELID.equals(m_tabValue))
        {
            if (m_rendered2 == false) 
            {
                m_rendered2 = true;
                m_tabValue = TAB_2_SELID;
            }
            else if (m_rendered3 == false)
            {
                m_rendered3 = true;
                m_tabValue = TAB_3_SELID;
            }
            else if (m_rendered4 == false)
            {
                m_rendered4 = true;
                m_tabValue = TAB_4_SELID;
            }
        }
    }
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Place components at begin/end of tabbed line

The component TABBEDPANE provides an area at the beginning (TABBEDAREABEGIN) and at the end (TABBEAREAEND) of the tabbed line, in which you can place one own component. (Of course you can e.g. also add a PANE component and several components inside the PANE component.)

Typical use case: you want to add some more additional tab instances by some "add"-icon.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedArea}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedArea}" >
<t:row id="g_49" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_59" value="#{d.DemoTabbedArea.tabValue}" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedareabegin id="g_82" >
<t:icon id="g_75" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedArea.onAddNewCarBeforeAction}" image="/images/iconssvg/add_16x16.svg" />
</t:tabbedareabegin>
<t:tabbedareaend id="g_6" >
<t:icon id="g_83" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedArea.onAddNewCarAction}" image="/images/iconssvg/add_16x16.svg" />
</t:tabbedareaend>
<t:repeat id="g_2" listbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedArea.carList}" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_3" text=".{id}" >
<t:row id="g_67" >
<t:field id="g_5" flush="true" labeltext="Id" text=".{id}" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_69" >
<t:field id="g_70" labeltext="Manufacturer" text=".{manufacturer}" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_72" >
<t:field id="g_73" labeltext="Type" text=".{type}" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_77" coldistance="5" >
<t:formattedfield id="g_78" format="int" labeltext="Power" value=".{power}" width="100%" />
<t:formattedfield id="g_80" format="int" labeltext="Max speed" value=".{maxSpeed}" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
</t:repeat>
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.List;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedArea}")

public class DemoTabbedArea
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public class CarListItem extends Object implements java.io.Serializable
    {
        String i_id;
        int i_maxSpeed;
        int i_power;
        String i_manufacturer;
        String i_type;
        public int getMaxSpeed() { return i_maxSpeed; }
        public void setMaxSpeed(int value) { this.i_maxSpeed = value; }
        public int getPower() { return i_power; }
        public void setPower(int value) { this.i_power = value; }
        public String getManufacturer() { return i_manufacturer; }
        public void setManufacturer(String value) { this.i_manufacturer = value; }
        public String getId() { return i_id; }
        public void setId(String value) { this.i_id = value; }
        public String getType() { return i_type; }
        public void setType(String value) { this.i_type = value; }
    }


    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    List<CarListItem> m_carList = new ArrayList<CarListItem>();
    int m_tabValue;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoTabbedArea(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
        CarListItem car = new CarListItem();
        car.setId("HD-CC 6999");
        car.setManufacturer("Mercedes");
        car.setType("Vito Tourer");
        m_carList.add(car);
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demotabbedarea.xml"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoTabbedArea}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public List<CarListItem> getCarList() { return m_carList; }

    public void onAddNewCarBeforeAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        CarListItem car = new CarListItem();
        car.setId("...new Id...");
        m_carList.add(0,car);
        m_tabValue = 0;
    }

    public void onAddNewCarAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        CarListItem car = new CarListItem();
        car.setId("...new Id...");
        m_carList.add(car);
        m_tabValue = m_carList.size()-1;
    }

    public int getTabValue() { return m_tabValue; }
    public void setTabValue(int value) { this.m_tabValue = value; }
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Hotkey Navigation

You can assign HOTKEY definitions to inidividual tabs.

As you see in the example, there are equal definitions used for different tabs (e.g. ctrl-1 is used both in the top-TABBEDPANE and in the bottom-TABBEDPANE).

The hotkey management first tries to resolve the definition, in which the current focus is located. Otherwise the first definition will be used.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedPaneHotkey}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedpane id="g_3" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_4" hotkey="ctrl-shift-49" padding="10" text="Left /ctrl-shift-1" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Some field" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_7" requestfocus="creation" width="100" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_8" hotkey="ctrl-shift-50" padding="10" text="Middle /ctrl-shift-2" >
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:label id="g_10" text="Some field" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_11" width="120" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
<t:tabbedpanetab id="g_12" hotkey="ctrl-shift-51" padding="10" text="Right /ctrl-shift-3" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:label id="g_14" text="Some field" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_15" width="140" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedpanetab>
</t:tabbedpane>
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_31" height="20" />
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

public class DemoTabbedPaneHotkey extends PageBean
{
    public DemoTabbedPaneHotkey(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)

        super(dispatcher);
    }
}

Tabs arranged at bottom

By default the "tabs" of a TABBEDPANE component are arranged on the top.

By using TABBEDPANE-TABPLACEMENT you can define that the tabs are arranged at the bottom.

When using the tab on the bottom then the "*_bottom" style class definitions are used. I.e. where the normal tabbed pane is using style class "risctabbedpane", the bottom-side arrangement now uses "risctabbedpane_bottom" - same with "risctabbedpane_flat" and "risctabbedpane_flat_bottom", etc.

This is the XML layout definition:

Tab Pane (server side)

Tabbed Line Container

The TABBEDLINECONTAINER components (what a nice name...!) is a tab component, that is simple to use - and powerful.

From first point of view it is very similar to the TABBEDPANE component, but there are some significant differences:

(.) Only the TAB-content is shown that is currently selected. Each selection of a tab is sent to the server side - and the corresponding content is shown.
This is quite important from scalability point of view. With a TABBEDPANE all contained tab-content is loaded to the client, also the content that is not shown at all. With a TABBEDLINECONTAINER component only the currently visible content is sent to the client side.
(.) All the painting of the tabs is nicely control-able through various BGPAINT attributes.
(.) The TABBEDLINECONTAINER internally consists out of a TABBEDLINE that is managing a content container.

The currently selected tab can be bound to a bean property by using the VALUE attribute. In addition you can bind the action listener to the component, so that you get a Select-event-notification every time the user switches to a new tab.

Please note:
(.) the BGPAINT attribute is affecting the whole component - if you only want to address the contained container component use INNERBGPAINT
(.) the BORDER and PADDING attribute are affecting the inner container component (that is placed below the tab-line on the top).

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainer}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainer id="g_3" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainer.onTabbedLineContainerAction}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" value="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainer.tabValue}" width="100%" distanceleftwidth="0" distancerightwidth="100%" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_4" text="Name" tooltip="Tooltip for name" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Title" width="100" />

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.defaultscreens.Statusbar;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.util.ClientTestLog;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.util.IClientLogAware;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainer}")

public class DemoTabbedLineContainer
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoTabbedLineContainer(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // set/get-properties for the form fields...
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    protected int m_tabValue;
    public int getTabValue() { return m_tabValue; }
    public void setTabValue(int value) { m_tabValue = value; }

    protected String m_mobile;
    public String getMobile() { return m_mobile; }
    public void setMobile(String value) { m_mobile = value; }

    protected String m_telephone;
    public String getTelephone() { return m_telephone; }
    public void setTelephone(String value) { m_telephone = value; }

    protected String m_country;
    public String getCountry() { return m_country; }
    public void setCountry(String value) { m_country = value; }

    protected String m_town;
    public String getTown() { return m_town; }
    public void setTown(String value) { m_town = value; }

    protected String m_zipCode;
    public String getZipCode() { return m_zipCode; }
    public void setZipCode(String value) { m_zipCode = value; }

    protected String m_street;
    public String getStreet() { return m_street; }
    public void setStreet(String value) { m_street = value; }

    protected String m_title;
    public String getTitle() { return m_title; }
    public void setTitle(String value) { m_title = value; }

    protected String m_lastName = "Casa";
    public String getLastName() { return m_lastName; }
    public void setLastName(String value) { m_lastName = value; }

    protected String m_firstName = "Captain";
    public String getFirstName() { return m_firstName; }
    public void setFirstName(String value) { m_firstName = value; }
    
    public void onTabbedLineContainerAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputMessage("TabbedLineContainerAction: " + event.toString());
    }

    public void onSet2(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_tabValue = 2;
    }

    
    
}

...with close icons

It is possible to provide close-icons on each tab - use the corresponding attribute WITHCLOSEICON that is available with the component TABBEDLINECONTAINERTAB.

When clickign onto a close button then a corresponding action listener is triggered on serve side - the event being an instance of class BaseActionEventTabClose.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainer id="g_3" height="100" value="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.selectedIndex}" width="100%" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_4" text="Left" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Left content" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedlinecontainertab>
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_7" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.onMiddleAction}" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.middleRendered}" text="Middle" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_9" text="Middle content" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedlinecontainertab>
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_10" actionListener="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.onRightAction}" rendered="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.rightRendered}" text="Right" withcloseicon="true" >
<t:row id="g_11" >

</t:row>

<t:row id="g_19" >
<t:label id="g_20" text="Selected Index" width="100" />
<t:label id="g_21" text="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon.selectedIndex}" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.events.BaseActionEventTabClose;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon}")

public class DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
   
    int m_selectedIndex = 0;
    public int getSelectedIndex() { return m_selectedIndex; }
    public void setSelectedIndex(int value) { this.m_selectedIndex = value; }

    public void onRightAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (event instanceof BaseActionEventTabClose)
        {
            m_rightRendered = false;
            m_selectedIndex = 0;
        }
    }

    public void onMiddleAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (event instanceof BaseActionEventTabClose)
        {
            m_middleRendered = false;
            m_selectedIndex = 0;
        }
    }

    boolean m_rightRendered = true;
    public boolean getRightRendered() { return m_rightRendered; }
    public void setRightRendered(boolean value) { this.m_rightRendered = value; }

    boolean m_middleRendered = true;
    public boolean getMiddleRendered() { return m_middleRendered; }
    public void setMiddleRendered(boolean value) { this.m_middleRendered = value; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoTabbedLineContainerWithCloseIcon(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Usage of Selection Id

by default the VALUE of the TABBEDLINE (or TABBEDLINTECONTAINER) reflects the index of the currently selected item.

But: you can also define a SELECTIONID on item level. In this case the VALUE reflects the currently selected selecition id value.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId}" rowdistance="20" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:tabbedline id="g_3" value="#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId.tlvalue}" >
<t:tabbedlinetab id="g_4" selectionid="LEFT" text="Left" />
<t:tabbedlinetab id="g_5" selectionid="MIDDLE" text="Middle" />
<t:tabbedlinetab id="g_6" selectionid="RIGHT" text="Right" />
</t:tabbedline>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainer id="g_8" value="#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId.tlvalue}" width="300" >
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_9" selectionid="LEFT" text="Left" >
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_11" text="Left" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedlinecontainertab>
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_12" selectionid="MIDDLE" text="Middle" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:label id="g_14" text="Middle" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedlinecontainertab>
<t:tabbedlinecontainertab id="g_15" selectionid="RIGHT" text="Right" >
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:label id="g_17" text="Right" />
</t:row>
</t:tabbedlinecontainertab>
</t:tabbedlinecontainer>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:label id="g_19" text="Selected Tab" width="100" />
<t:combobox id="g_20" flush="true" value="#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId.tlvalue}" width="100" >
<t:comboboxitem id="g_21" text="Left" value="LEFT" />
<t:comboboxitem id="g_22" text="Middle" value="MIDDLE" />
<t:comboboxitem id="g_23" text="Right" value="RIGHT" />
</t:combobox>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId}")

public class DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    String m_tlvalue = "MIDDLE";
    public String getTlvalue() { return m_tlvalue; }
    public void setTlvalue(String value) { this.m_tlvalue = value; }

    public DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demotabbedlinetabselectionid.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoTabbedLineTabSelectionId}"; }

}

Dynamically assembled

This example shows how to dynamically assemble a TABBEDLINECONTAINER - each tab showing a page bean.

There is "nothing special" to pay attention to:

(.) use ROWDYNAMICCONTENT to open up an area in which the content is dynamically created
(.) build the dynamic content on Java code side (here: directly called from the constructor)
(.) create a ROWBAGEBEANINCLUDE component insde each tab and bind it to a page bean

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer}" >
<t:rowdynamiccontent id="g_3" contentbinding="#{d.DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer.dynContent}" />
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.TABBEDLINECONTAINERNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer}")

public class DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding m_dynContent = new ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding();

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);
        renderContent();
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demodynamictabbedlinecontainer.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoDynamicTabbedlineContainer}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding getDynContent() { return m_dynContent; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    private void renderContent()
    {
        TABBEDLINECONTAINERNode tlc = new TABBEDLINECONTAINERNode()
                .setWidth("100%")
                .setHeight("100%");
        {
            TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode tlct = new TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode()
                    .setText("Hello world");
            tlc.addSubNode(tlct);
            ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode rin = new ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode()
                    .bindPagebeanbinding(new DemoHelloWorld(getOwningDispatcher()));
            tlct.addSubNode(rin);
        }
        {
            TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode tlct = new TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode()
                    .setText("Mini Spreadsheet");
            tlc.addSubNode(tlct);
            ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode rin = new ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode()
                    .bindPagebeanbinding(new DemoMinispread(getOwningDispatcher()));
            tlct.addSubNode(rin);
        }
        {
            TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode tlct = new TABBEDLINECONTAINERTABNode()
                    .setText("Budget calculation");
            tlc.addSubNode(tlct);
            ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode rin = new ROWPAGEBEANINCLUDENode()
                    .bindPagebeanbinding(new DemoBudget(getOwningDispatcher()));
            tlct.addSubNode(rin);
        }
        m_dynContent.setContentNode(tlc);
    }
}

Tabs arranged at bottom

By default the "tabs" of a TABBEDLINECONTAINER component are arranged on the top.

By using TABBEDLINECONTAINER-TABPLACEMENT you can define that the tabs are arranged at the bottom.

When using the tab on the bottom then the "*_bottom" style class definitions are used. I.e. where the normal tabbed pane is using style class "risctabbedpane", the bottom-side arrangement now uses "risctabbedpane_bottom" - same with "risctabbedpane_flat" and "risctabbedpane_flat_bottom", etc.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

Pile

Pile component

The PILE component is used for stacking components vertically.

You could do the same with a PANE component, arranging each content within a ROW component - but the PILE does automatically arrange it this way.

Pleas note: by default each contained component gets assigned a width of 100% so that it fills the pile. You of course can assign an individual width to each contained component.

The pile is e.g. useful for traditional LABEL-FIELD combinations, in which the LABEL is not integrated into the FIELD component.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.captaincasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoPile}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoPile}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:label id="g_37" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Some pile-label-field combinations" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_6" coldistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultcoldistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:pile id="g_8" width="100%" >
<t:label id="g_14" font="weight:bold" text="First name" />
<t:field id="g_12" text="Captain" />
</t:pile>
<t:pile id="g_16" width="100%" >
<t:label id="g_17" font="weight:bold" text="Last name" />
<t:field id="g_18" text="Case" />
</t:pile>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_20" coldistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultcoldistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:pile id="g_21" width="100%" >
<t:label id="g_22" font="weight:bold" text="Street" />
<t:field id="g_23" text="Hauptstraße" />
</t:pile>
<t:pile id="g_25" >
<t:label id="g_26" font="weight:bold" text="Number" />
<t:field id="g_27" text="13" width="100" />
</t:pile>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_29" coldistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultcoldistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:pile id="g_33" >
<t:label id="g_34" font="weight:bold" text="Postal code" />
<t:field id="g_35" text="69245" width="100" />
</t:pile>
<t:pile id="g_30" width="100%" >
<t:label id="g_31" font="weight:bold" text="Town" />
<t:field id="g_32" text="Hauptstraße" />
</t:pile>
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_5" height="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistancebig@&#39;]}" />
<t:row id="g_39" >
<t:label id="g_40" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Some buttons" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_42" >
<t:pile id="g_7" rowdistance="2" >
<t:button id="g_44" text="Button 1" />
<t:button id="g_46" text="Button 2 with longer text" />
<t:button id="g_48" text="Button 3" />
<t:button id="g_50" text="Button 4" />
</t:pile>

<t:row id="g_59" >
<t:label id="g_60" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Some buttons with decoration" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_52" >
<t:pile id="g_53" background="#00000004" border="#c0c0c0" padding="10" rounding="10" rowdistance="2" >
<t:button id="g_54" text="Button 1" />
<t:button id="g_55" text="Button 2 with longer text" />
<t:button id="g_56" text="Button 3" />
<t:button id="g_57" text="Button 4" />
</t:pile>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

Sizeable Pane

In each foldable pane a SIZEABLEPANE component is placed: on the bottom of each you see a shaded line that you can drag and drop for changing the height of the pane.

Please note, when using the component SIZEABLEPANE: the components that are placed into the pane need to be percentage-sized, otherwise no sizing will be enabled - it does not make sense to have dynamic sizing around fix-sized content. In the example it is the foldable pane with a height of 100% that is the one to be sized.

The height is returned in pixel values, taking into consideration that there is a certain scaling on client side. By using the attribute FLUSH you can define that height updates are sent immediately after having changed the height.

The component is somehow similar with the SPLITPANE component, but: each SIZEABLEPANE is sized independent from other panes - whereas the SPLITPANE component always sizes (exactly) two panes that are contained.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSizeablepane}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Top Height" width="120" />
<t:field id="g_4" flush="true" text="#{d.DemoSizeablepane.topSize}" width="100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Bottom Height" width="120" />
<t:field id="g_7" flush="true" text="#{d.DemoSizeablepane.bottomSize}" width="100" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_8" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:sizeablepane id="g_10" flush="true" height="#{d.DemoSizeablepane.topSize}" sizersize="10" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_12" enabled="false" height="100%" innerpadding="0" text="Top" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:sizeablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:sizeablepane id="g_14" flush="true" height="#{d.DemoSizeablepane.bottomSize}" sizerbackground="#00000000" sizersize="10" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_15" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_16" enabled="false" height="100%" innerpadding="0" text="Bottom" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:sizeablepane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.managedbean.IDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoSizeablepane}")

public class DemoSizeablepane 
    extends PageBean
{
    public DemoSizeablepane(IDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

    protected String m_bottomSize = "50%;200";
    public String getBottomSize() { return m_bottomSize; }
    public void setBottomSize(String value) { m_bottomSize = value; }

    protected String m_topSize = "50%;200";
    public String getTopSize() { return m_topSize; }
    public void setTopSize(String value) { m_topSize = value; }

}

Grid layout pane

Simple examples

The GRIDLAYOUTPANE is a layout component that internally opens up a matrix of areas.

The matrix is defined by the content of its GRIDLAYOUTROWS. Each element of a row is places into this matrix according to its position in the row and according to its definition of COLSPAN AND ROWSPAN.

The sizing of the matrix is automatically calculated so that the minimum size and the preferred size of each component is respected.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

One "leader" component drives width

In this example the fields with the red background drive the width sizing of the columns.

The corresponding fields are set to a certain width (e.g. "150"), the other fields are set to "1%". As result, due to the percentage sizing, the fields fill the whole column - but have a lower width as the leader-field in the same column.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutLeadingComponent}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutLeadingComponent}" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:gridlayoutpane id="g_7" coldistance="10" rowdistance="10" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_5" align="right" text="First" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_9" width="1%" />
<t:label id="g_20" align="right" text="First" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_24" width="1%" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_17" align="right" text="Second" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_12" background="#FFC0C0" width="100" />
<t:label id="g_21" align="right" text="Second" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_25" width="1%" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_18" align="right" text="Third" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_15" width="1%" />
<t:label id="g_22" align="right" text="Third" width="100+" />
<t:field id="g_26" background="#FFC0C0" width="150" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:gridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

Cross-synchronization of columns

This is something "unique": you can harmonize the sizing of grid layout panes so that they share their column layouts.

In the layout there are three grid layout panes. The column structure is harmonized by assigning each of them a SHAREMINSIZINGID attribute.

Please check: when updating the column content (e.g. by not rendering the second area and/or by changing the label of the last grid layout pane) then the update will be synchronized through all the grid layout panes!

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}" rowdistance="20" >
<t:row id="g_45" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_2" text="Some first grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_53" >
<t:gridlayoutpane id="g_54" coldistance="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" shareminsizingid="A" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_55" >
<t:label id="g_56" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_57" width="200" />
<t:label id="g_58" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_59" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_60" >
<t:label id="g_61" text="AAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_62" width="200" />
<t:label id="g_63" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_64" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:gridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_47" text="Some second grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_48" >
<t:checkbox id="g_43" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing.renderSecondPart}" text="Render the following part" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" rendered="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing.renderSecondPart}" >
<t:gridlayoutpane id="g_17" coldistance="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" shareminsizingid="A" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_18" >
<t:label id="g_19" text="AAAAAAAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_20" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_21" >
<t:label id="g_22" text="AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_23" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:gridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_50" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_6" text="Some third grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_25" >
<t:gridlayoutpane id="g_26" coldistance="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" shareminsizingid="A" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_27" >
<t:label id="g_28" text="A" />
<t:field id="g_29" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_30" >
<t:label id="g_31" text="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing.labelLast}" />
<t:field id="g_32" width="200" />
<t:label id="g_40" text="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing.labelLast}" />
<t:field id="g_41" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_51" >
<t:button id="g_34" actionListener="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing.onChangeLabelAction}" text="Change label" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:gridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}")

public class DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    final String M5 = "MMMMMA";
    final String M20 = "MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM";
    
    String m_labelLast = M5;
    boolean m_renderSecondPart = true;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demogridlayoutsharedsizing.xml"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public String getLabelLast() { return m_labelLast; }
    public void setLabelLast(String value) { this.m_labelLast = value; }

    public boolean getRenderSecondPart() { return m_renderSecondPart; }
    public void setRenderSecondPart(boolean value) { this.m_renderSecondPart = value; }

    public void onChangeLabelAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (m_labelLast == M5)
            m_labelLast = M20;
        else
            m_labelLast = M5;
    }
}

Cross-synchronization of columns - adaptive version

The same "harmonizing" of column sizes that is available in the GRIDLAYOUTPANE component is available as will within the ADAPTIVEGRIDLAYOUTPANE component.

In the example there are 3 instances of ADAPTIVEGRIDLAYOUTPANE - updating the column structure in one of them will automatically update the columns structure of the related ones.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2}" rowdistance="20" >
<t:row id="g_45" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_2" text="Some first grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:adaptivegridlayoutpane id="g_8" adaptivecolindices="400:1-1-1-1;600:2-2" coldistance="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" shareminsizingid="A" width="100%" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_9" >
<t:label id="g_10" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_5" width="200" />
<t:label id="g_36" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_37" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_12" >
<t:label id="g_13" text="AAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_14" width="200" />
<t:label id="g_38" text="AAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_39" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:adaptivegridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_47" text="Some second grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_48" >
<t:checkbox id="g_43" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2.renderSecondPart}" text="Render the following part" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" rendered="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2.renderSecondPart}" >
<t:adaptivegridlayoutpane id="g_17" adaptivecolindices="400:1-1-1-1;600:2-2" coldistance="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" shareminsizingid="A" width="100%" >
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_18" >
<t:label id="g_19" text="AAAAAAAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_20" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_21" >
<t:label id="g_22" text="AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA" />
<t:field id="g_23" width="200" />
</t:gridlayoutrow>
</t:adaptivegridlayoutpane>
</t:row>
</t:foldablepane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_50" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_6" text="Some third grid layout pane" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_25" >

<t:gridlayoutrow id="g_27" >
<t:label id="g_28" text="A" />

</t:gridlayoutrow>

<t:label id="g_40" text="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2.labelLast}" />

</t:gridlayoutrow>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}")

public class DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    final String M5 = "MMMMM";
    final String M20 = "MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM";
    
    String m_labelLast = M5;
    boolean m_renderSecondPart = true;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing2(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demogridlayoutsharedsizing.xml"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoGridLayoutSharedSizing}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public String getLabelLast() { return m_labelLast; }
    public void setLabelLast(String value) { this.m_labelLast = value; }

    public boolean getRenderSecondPart() { return m_renderSecondPart; }
    public void setRenderSecondPart(boolean value) { this.m_renderSecondPart = value; }

    public void onChangeLabelAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (m_labelLast == M5)
            m_labelLast = M20;
        else
            m_labelLast = M5;
    }
}

Applying shadows

All graphical components provide a SHADOW attribute.

The definition of the value internally consists out of 3 definitions:

1. the horizontal offset of the shadow
2. the vertical offset of the shadows
3. the blurring around the border of the shadow. If defining "0" then the border of the shadow is "exact!". If defining "4" then there is some blurring 2 with a size of 2 pixels on each side of the border line.

The shadow definition automatically updates the component's size: a margin is arranged around the component.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoShadow}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_1" >
<t:field id="g_7" shadow="hoffset:5;voffset:5;blur:5;color:#c0c0c0" text="Some field" width="150" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:button id="g_10" shadow="hoffset:5;voffset:5;blur:0;color:#800000" text="Some button" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:icon id="g_11" border="#00000010" image="/images/iconssvg/save.svg" imageheight="24" imagewidth="24" shadow="hoffset:3;voffset:3;blur:4;color:#c0c0c0" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:pane id="g_6" background="#00000010" height="100" shadow="hoffset:20;voffset:20;blur:20;color:#00008030" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:pane id="g_19" background="#00000010" height="100" shadow="hoffset:20;voffset:5;blur:20;color:#00008030" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_14" shadow="hoffset:8;voffset:8;blur:4;color:#c0c0c0" text="Some title" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

Background painting

BGPAINT command

There is a set of paint commands which you can use for pane components.

Using these paint commands you can...
(.) Draw colored rectangles
(.) Draw colored rectangles with a vetical or horizontal color change
(.) Draw rounded rectangles in the same way
(.) Paint images

Note: all this is the background of the pane, i.e. controls are placed on top of it.


Paint commands can be concatenated by building a semicolon separated list.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.demoBgpaint}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Vertical" width="150" />
<t:pane id="g_4" bgpaint="bgbackground(#00000000,#00000030,vertical)" height="100" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="Horizontal" width="150" />
<t:pane id="g_7" bgpaint="bgbackground(#00000000,#00000030,horizontal)" height="100" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_9" text="Command concatenation" width="150" />
<t:pane id="g_10" bgpaint="bgbackground(#00000000,#00000030,horizontal);bgbackground(#00000000,#00000030,vertical)" height="100" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_12" text="With image" width="150" />
<t:pane id="g_13" bgpaint="bgbackground(#680000,#F0F0F0,horizontal);bgimage(left,/images/icons/bigspeakerpressed.png);bgimage(right,/images/icons/bigspeakerpressed.png);" height="100" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_15" text="Text output" width="150" />
<t:pane id="g_16" bgpaint="bgbackground(#680000,#F0F0F0,horizontal);bgwrite(center,Hello world!);bgwrite(bottom,Hello world!,#FFFFFF80,20)" height="100" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

}

BGPAINT command with conditions

All BGPAINT commands can be combined with conditions:

The syntax is:

<command><condition>

The command is only executed if the condition is fulfilled.

There are the following conditions:

1. _focus
2. _nofocus
3. _empty
4. _enabled
5. _disabled

Please note: the BGPAINT commands should only be used for special background coloring within the component. They should not be used for general styling issues!

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoBgpaintConditions}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoBgpaintConditions}" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:label id="g_7" text="_focus" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_8" bgpaint="bgbackground_focus(#fee599)" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_11" text="_nofocus" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_12" bgpaint="bgbackground_nofocus(#e599fe)" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_15" text="_focus &amp; _nofocus" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_16" bgpaint="bgbackground_nofocus(#e599fe);bgbackground_focus(#fee599)" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_5" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:label id="g_19" text="_empty" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_20" bgpaint="bgbackground_empty(#fee599)" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_26" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_22" >
<t:label id="g_23" text="_enabled" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_24" bgpaint="bgbackground_enabled(#fee599)" enabled="#{d.DemoBgpaintConditions.fieldEnabled}" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_31" >
<t:label id="g_32" text="_disabled" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_33" bgpaint="bgbackground_disabled(#fee599)" enabled="#{d.DemoBgpaintConditions.fieldEnabled}" labeltext="Some field" width="200" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_27" >
<t:coldistance id="g_28" width="150" />
<t:link id="g_29" actionListener="#{d.DemoBgpaintConditions.onToggleEnabledAction}" text="Toggle enabled/disabled" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

Container sizing

Column distance in rows

The ROW components provides an attribute COLDISTANCE - which is the default horizontal distance between the contained components.

This is the horizontal counter part of the ROWDISTANCE attribute, that is provided in container components.

Row distance in panes

A pane is a container component, in which rows are placed. By default the rows follow one another, i.e. there is no vertical distance between the rows. You can specify a general distance that is placed between the rows by using the attribute ROWDISTANCE.

Please note: there is also a component ROWDISTANCE that can be placed into a container. If using the component ROWDISTANCE then also for this component an additional distance is calculated, depending from the value of the pane container's ROWDISTANCE attribute.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >

package workplace;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

Cut percentage height/width

You can use the attribute CUTWIDTH and CUTHEIGHT in order to influence the PANE's behavior when being sized with percentage width/height.

By default the assignment of a percentage size (e.g. width) has the following consequences:

1. the controls receives the width according to the current screen size / page constellation
2. if the width is not sufficient then the width automatically is expanded to show the inner content

So a percentage size by default means, that the control will always be rendered with its minimum size, if the percentage size is not sufficient.

By setting CUTWIDTH / CUTHEIGHT to "true" you override this default behavior: the percentage size is not interpreted as strict size, so that the content of the pane is cut when exceeding the percentage size.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoPaneCutWidth}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:textpane id="g_3" text="Resize the screen and observer the different sizing behavior of the two PANE instances:" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:pane id="g_5" background="#c0c0c0" height="25%" padding="5" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" width="50%" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:label id="g_7" text="Width=50%, height=25% - default sizing" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:button id="g_9" text="button" />
<t:button id="g_10" text="button" />
<t:button id="g_11" text="button" />
