This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoAnimateChangeOfSize}")

public class DemoAnimateChangeOfSize
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    public void onTogglePaneWidthPercPixel(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if ("240".equals(m_paneWidthPercPixel))
            m_paneWidthPercPixel = "100%";
        else
            m_paneWidthPercPixel = "240";
    }

    String m_paneWidthPercPixel = "240";
    public String getPaneWidthPercPixel() { return m_paneWidthPercPixel; }
    public void setPaneWidthPercPixel(String value) { this.m_paneWidthPercPixel = value; }

    public void onTogglePaneWidthPerc(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if ("50%".equals(m_paneWidthPerc))
            m_paneWidthPerc = "100%";
        else
            m_paneWidthPerc = "50%";
    }

    String m_paneWidthPerc = "50%";
    public String getPaneWidthPerc() { return m_paneWidthPerc; }
    public void setPaneWidthPerc(String value) { this.m_paneWidthPerc = value; }

    public void onTogglePaneWidth(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (m_paneWidth == 240)
            m_paneWidth = 390;
        else
            m_paneWidth = 240;
    }

    int m_paneWidth = 240;
    public int getPaneWidth() { return m_paneWidth; }
    public void setPaneWidth(int value) { this.m_paneWidth = value; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Listener to the user of the page bean. */
    public interface IListener
    {
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    private IListener m_listener;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoAnimateChangeOfSize(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoanimatechangeofsize.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoAnimateChangeOfSize}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Initialization of the bean. Add any parameter that is required within your scenario. */
    public void prepare(IListener listener)
    {
        m_listener = listener;
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Alignment in Rows

Within a row several components can be arranged - each one having a different height. In the example the TEXTAREA on the very right of each row is having the highest height, and as consequence is driving the whole row's height.

The default vertical positioning of components inside a row is "center". This means: if the component does not occupy all the height that comes from the row, then it is automatically put into the vertical center.

By using the attribute ROWALIGNMENTY you can override this behaviour.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_3" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" objectbinding="#{d.demoRowalignment}">
  <t:row id="g_4" >
    <t:label id="g_5" text="Center" width="50" />
    <t:field id="g_6" width="50" />
    <t:button id="g_7" text="OK" />
    <t:tabbedpane id="g_8" height="50" width="100" >
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_9" text="Tab" />
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_10" text="Tab" />
    </t:tabbedpane>
    <t:textarea id="g_11" height="100" width="100%" />
  </t:row>
  <t:row id="g_12" >
    <t:label id="g_13" rowalignmenty="top" text="Top" width="50" />
    <t:field id="g_14" rowalignmenty="top" width="50" />
    <t:button id="g_15" rowalignmenty="top" text="OK" />
    <t:tabbedpane id="g_16" height="50" rowalignmenty="top" width="100" >
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_17" text="Tab" />
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_18" text="Tab" />
    </t:tabbedpane>
    <t:textarea id="g_19" height="100" width="100%" />
  </t:row>
  <t:row id="g_20" >
    <t:label id="g_21" rowalignmenty="bottom" text="Bottom" width="50" />
    <t:field id="g_22" rowalignmenty="bottom" width="50" />
    <t:button id="g_23" rowalignmenty="bottom" text="OK" />
    <t:tabbedpane id="g_24" height="50" rowalignmenty="bottom" width="100" >
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_25" text="Tab" />
      <t:tabbedpanetab id="g_26" text="Tab" />
    </t:tabbedpane>
    <t:textarea id="g_27" height="100" width="100%" />
  </t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

public class DemoRowalignment extends PageBean
{
    public DemoRowalignment(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }
}

Scroll Pane - Extended Functions

Scroll to certain Position

Within the layout that is placed into a SCROLLPANE component, you can define SCROLLANCHOR components.

These SCROLLANCHOR components are invisible components. Their only purpose: they provide a trigger, so that you can make the SCROLLPANE scrolling to the anchor's position from the server side.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:button id="g_3" actionListener="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.onScroll1}" text="To Position 1" />
<t:coldistance id="g_4" width="5" />
<t:button id="g_5" actionListener="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.onScroll2}" text="To Position 2" />
<t:coldistance id="g_6" width="5" />
<t:button id="g_7" actionListener="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.onScroll3}" text="To Position 3" />
<t:coldistance id="g_8" width="5" />
<t:button id="g_9" actionListener="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.onScroll4}" text="To Position 4" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_10" height="20" />
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_12" border="#00000030" height="100%" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:scrollanchor id="g_14" scrolltrigger="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.trigger1}" />
<t:label id="g_15" focusable="true" font="size:50" text="Scroll Position 1" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_16" height="300" />
<t:row id="g_17" >
<t:scrollanchor id="g_18" scrolltrigger="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.trigger2}" />
<t:label id="g_19" focusable="true" font="size:20" text="Scroll Position 2" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_20" height="600" />
<t:row id="g_21" >
<t:coldistance id="g_22" width="1000" />
<t:scrollanchor id="g_23" scrolltrigger="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.trigger3}" />
<t:label id="g_24" focusable="true" font="size:20" text="Scroll Position 3" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_25" height="600" />
<t:row id="g_26" >
<t:pane id="g_27" background="#00000030" height="200" padding="50" width="100%" >
<t:rowdistance id="g_28" height="100%" />
<t:row id="g_29" >
<t:coldistance id="g_30" width="200" />
<t:scrollanchor id="g_31" scrolltrigger="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor.trigger4}" />
<t:label id="g_32" focusable="true" font="size:20" text="Scroll Position 4" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.util.Trigger;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollAnchor}")

public class DemoScrollAnchor
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    protected Trigger m_trigger1 = new Trigger();
    protected Trigger m_trigger2 = new Trigger();
    protected Trigger m_trigger3 = new Trigger();
    protected Trigger m_trigger4 = new Trigger();
    
    public DemoScrollAnchor(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);  
        m_trigger4.trigger();
    }

    public Trigger getTrigger1() { return m_trigger1; }
    public void setTrigger1(Trigger value) { m_trigger1 = value; }

    public Trigger getTrigger2() { return m_trigger2; }
    public void setTrigger2(Trigger value) { m_trigger2 = value; }
    
    public Trigger getTrigger3() { return m_trigger3; }
    public void setTrigger3(Trigger value) { m_trigger3 = value; }
    
    public Trigger getTrigger4() { return m_trigger4; }
    public void setTrigger4(Trigger value) { m_trigger4 = value; }

    public void onScroll1(ActionEvent event) { m_trigger1.trigger(); }
    public void onScroll2(ActionEvent event) { m_trigger2.trigger(); }
    public void onScroll3(ActionEvent event) { m_trigger3.trigger(); }
    public void onScroll4(ActionEvent event) { m_trigger4.trigger(); }

}

Scroll to end of text

In this example a SCROLLANCHOR is set into the SCROLLPANE - directly below the TEXTPANE component, showing the protocol.

Every time a new message is added to the protocol, the SCROLLANCHOR is triggered.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoMessageProtocol}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:button id="g_3" actionListener="#{d.DemoMessageProtocol.onAddMessage}" doubleclickenabled="true" text="Add a message" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_5" border="#808080" height="100%" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:textpane id="g_7" text="#{d.DemoMessageProtocol.message}" width="100%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:scrollanchor id="g_9" scrolltrigger="#{d.DemoMessageProtocol.scrollTrigger}" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.util.Trigger;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoMessageProtocol}")

public class DemoMessageProtocol
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    Trigger m_scrollTrigger = new Trigger();
    String m_message = 
        "Message Protocol\n\n" +
        "\n" +
        "Fill the protocol by clicking the button.\n" +
        "The text of the protocol will always scroll to the\n" +
        "end, so that the most up to date information is available.\n\n\n";
    int m_counter = 1;
    
    public DemoMessageProtocol(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public Trigger getScrollTrigger() { return m_scrollTrigger; }

    public String getMessage() { return m_message; }
    public void setMessage(String value) { this.m_message = value; }

    public void onAddMessage(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_message += "Button pressed " + m_counter + "\n";
        m_counter++;
        m_scrollTrigger.trigger();
    }
    
}

Scrollbar Mode

By using the attributes HORIZONTALSCROLLMODE and VERTICALSCROLLMODE you can control the scrolling behavior of the SCROLLPANE component.

Please note: the attribute value "autowithresize" is reserved for FIXGRID components only - it cannot be applied with SCROLLPANE components.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPane}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Normal Scrolling" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_5" border="#00000030" height="100" width="200" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:label id="g_7" font="size:100" text="A very big text..." />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:label id="g_9" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Only vertical" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_11" border="#00000030" height="100" horizontalscrollmode="hidden" width="200" >
<t:row id="g_12" >
<t:label id="g_13" font="size:100" text="A very big text..." />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_15" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Only horizontal" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_17" border="#00000030" height="100" verticalscrollmode="hidden" width="200" >
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:label id="g_19" font="size:100" text="A very big text..." />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollPane}")

public class DemoScrollPane
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    public DemoScrollPane(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }
}

Scroll to top/bottom events

The SCROLLPANE component sends certain scroll events to the server-side:

1. when defining WITHSCROLLEVENTTOP to "true" then the scroll pane sends an event when the user scrolls from/to the top scroll position.

2. when defining WITHSCROLLEVENTBOTTOM to "true" then the scroll pane sends an event when the user scrolls from/to the bottom scroll position.

You may use these events to update e.g. some header or footer area - or to receive some event that the user scrolled to the end, e.g. when presenting legal texts (license terms...).

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoScrollpaneScrollListener}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_57" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollpaneScrollListener}" >
<t:row id="g_15" >
<t:textpane id="g_16" text="Scroll the content below and observe the header area:" width="100%" />
</t:row>

<t:row id="g_80" coldistance="5" >

<t:field id="g_48" labeltext="Some field" text="Some field" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.events.BaseActionEventScroll;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollpaneScrollListener}")

public class DemoScrollpaneScrollListener
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    boolean m_renderedExtendedHeadline = true;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScrollpaneScrollListener(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscrollpanescrolllistener.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScrollpaneScrollListener}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public void onScrollAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (event instanceof BaseActionEventScroll)
        {
            BaseActionEventScroll e = (BaseActionEventScroll)event;
            if ("top".equals(e.getPosition()))
            {
                if (e.checkIfPositionWasLeft() == true)
                    m_renderedExtendedHeadline = false;
                else
                    m_renderedExtendedHeadline = true;
            }
        }
    }

    public boolean getRenderedExtendedHeadline() { return m_renderedExtendedHeadline; }
    public void setRenderedExtendedHeadline(boolean value) { this.m_renderedExtendedHeadline = value; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Dynamic loading of content

The SCROLLPANE fires a BaseActionEventScroll-Event when reaching the bottom scroll position - and when having set WITHSCROLLEVENTBOTTOM to true.

In the example the result of the server-side event processing is that additional 10 items are appended to the dynamic content within the SCROLLPANE content.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollNotifier}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Scroll to the end of the following SCROLLPANE:" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_5" actionListener="#{d.DemoScrollNotifier.onScrollAction}" border="#00000030" height="300" width="300" withscrolleventbottom="true" >
<t:rowdynamiccontent id="g_14" contentbinding="#{d.DemoScrollNotifier.content}" />
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_12" text="... End of loaded data ..." />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.IMAGENode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.LABELNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.PANENode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.ROWNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.events.BaseActionEventScroll;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollNotifier}")

public class DemoScrollNotifier
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    PANENode m_paneNode = new PANENode();
    int m_renderIndex = 0;
    ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding m_content = new ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding();

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScrollNotifier(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);       
        m_paneNode.addAttribute("id","PANE");
        m_paneNode.setRowdistance(5);
        renderAppend();
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscrollnotifier.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScrollNotifier}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding getContent() { return m_content; }

    public void onScrollAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        if (event instanceof BaseActionEventScroll)
        {
            BaseActionEventScroll e = (BaseActionEventScroll)event;
            if ("bottom".equals(e.getPosition()) && e.checkIfPositionWasReached() == true)
            {
                renderAppend();
            }
        }
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    private void renderAppend()
    {
        // Pleae note:
        // Ids are explicitly assigned! Otherwise the client interprets all
        // controls as new controls, and as consequence re-renders the full dynamic
        // content.
        // with passing the ids (and keeping them constant!) the client
        // know that some content already was available before any only renders
        // the new content.
        for (int i=0; i<10; i++)
        {
            ROWNode rn = new ROWNode();
            m_paneNode.addSubNode(rn);
            rn.addAttribute("id","ROW"+m_renderIndex);
            rn.setColdistance(5); 
            IMAGENode in = new IMAGENode();
            rn.addSubNode(in);
            in.addAttribute("id","IM"+m_renderIndex);
            in.setImage("/images/pictures/photo"+i+".gif");
            in.setWidth(50);
            in.setHeight(50);
            in.setKeepratio(false);
            LABELNode ln = new LABELNode();
            rn.addSubNode(ln);
            ln.addAttribute("id","LA"+m_renderIndex);
            ln.setText("Text of item " + m_renderIndex);
            m_renderIndex++;
        }
        m_content.setContentNode(m_paneNode);
    }
}

Scroll by drag/drop

By using the attribute SCROLLPANE-TOUCHSCROLLSUPPORT you may defined, that the scroll pane content can not only be scrolled using the scroll bars or the mouse wheel - but can also be scrolled by dragging and dropping with the mouse.

(This function is not activated for mobile or tabled environments - there the scrolling is automatically done by sliding with the finger.)

This is the XML layout definition:

Height or Width following content

If you do not define the HEIGHT or the WIDTH definition of a SCROLLPANE, then the SCROLLPANE will take the corresponding size that is required by its content.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneSizing}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Height set, width not set" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_5" border="#00000030" height="200" padding="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue[&#39;@defaultrowdistance@&#39;]}" width="byContent" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:label id="g_7" text="Some content" width="100" />
<t:textarea id="g_8" height="100" width="300" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:label id="g_10" text="Some content" width="100" />
<t:textarea id="g_11" height="100" width="300" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_12" />
<t:row id="g_13" >

</t:row>
<t:row id="g_15" >

Synchronized Scrolling (Java Client only)

Scroll the central scroll pane - either the scroll pane above or the scroll pane left will scroll as well.

You may use the attributes SCROLLREFERENCEHORIZONTAL and/or SCROLLREFERENCEVERTICAL in order to bind the own scrolling state of a SCROLLPANE to the scrolling of another SCROLLPANE.

Please pay attention: you must assure that the sizing of the corresponding SCROLLPANEs is correct.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:pane id="g_3" border="#800000" height="100%" padding="1" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:coldistance id="g_5" width="100" />
<t:colline id="g_6" background="#800000" height="100" width="1" />
<t:pane id="g_7" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_9" background="#f0f0f0" height="130" scrollreferencehorizontal="SCROLLMASTER" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:drawarea id="g_11" drawcommands="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference.bgpaintHorizontal}" height="100%" width="2000" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
<t:rowline id="g_12" background="#800000" height="1" />
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:pane id="g_14" height="100%" width="100" >
<t:row id="g_15" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_16" background="#f0f0f0" height="100%" scrollreferencevertical="SCROLLMASTER" width="130" >
<t:row id="g_17" >
<t:drawarea id="g_18" drawcommands="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference.bgpaintVertical}" height="2000" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:pane>
<t:colline id="g_19" background="#800000" height="100%" width="1" />
<t:scrollpane id="SCROLLMASTER" background="#FFFFFF" height="100%" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_20" >
<t:pane id="g_21" height="2000" width="2000" />
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.pagebean.PageBean;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}")

public class DemoScrollPaneReference
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    String m_bgpaintVertical = "";
    public String getBgpaintVertical() { return m_bgpaintVertical; }
    public void setBgpaintVertical(String value) { this.m_bgpaintVertical = value; }

    String m_bgpaintHorizontal = "";
    public String getBgpaintHorizontal() { return m_bgpaintHorizontal; }
    public void setBgpaintHorizontal(String value) { this.m_bgpaintHorizontal = value; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    /* Listener to the user of the page bean. */
    public interface IListener
    {
    }
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    private IListener m_listener;
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScrollPaneReference(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
        for (int i=0; i<20; i++)
        {
            int y = i * 100;
            if (i != 0) m_bgpaintVertical += "line(0,"+y+",100,"+y+",1,#000000);";
            m_bgpaintVertical += "write(5,"+(y+5)+","+y+",lefttop);";
            int x = i * 100;
            if (i != 0) m_bgpaintHorizontal += "line("+x+",0,"+x+",100,1,#000000);";
            m_bgpaintHorizontal += "write("+(x+5)+",5,"+x+",lefttop);";
        }
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscrollpanereference.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Initialization of the bean. Add any parameter that is required within your scenario. */
    public void prepare(IListener listener)
    {
        m_listener = listener;
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Set/get Scroll Position

The SCROLLPANE component and the ROWBODYPANE component provide an attribute SCROLLPOSITION. If set (use expression!) then the current scroll position of the component is transferred with each server request. Vice versa, if you explicitly set the scroll position on server side, then the component will scroll accordingly.

The value that is transferred follows the format "x;y", you may decode the value on server side by using "ValueManager.decodeStraighIntCSV()".

This is the XML layout definition:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.defaultscreens.Statusbar;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.managedbean.IDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.pagebean.PageBean;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoRowBodyPaneScrollPosition}")

public class DemoRowBodyPaneScrollPosition
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    String m_scrollPosition;
    public String getScrollPosition() { return m_scrollPosition; }
    public void setScrollPosition(String value) { this.m_scrollPosition = value; }

    public void onSyncAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("Current scroll position: " + m_scrollPosition);
    }

    public void onScrollAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_scrollPosition = "20;20";
    }

    public DemoRowBodyPaneScrollPosition(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
        m_scrollPosition = "100;100";
    }
    
    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demorowbodypanescrollposition.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoRowBodyPaneScrollPosition}"; }

}

Synchronized scrolling

Scroll the central scroll pane - either the scroll pane above or the scroll pane left will scroll as well.

You may use the attributes SCROLLREFERENCEHORIZONTAL and/or SCROLLREFERENCEVERTICAL in order to bind the own scrolling state of a SCROLLPANE to the scrolling of another SCROLLPANE.

Please pay attention: you must assure that the sizing of the corresponding SCROLLPANEs is correct.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}" >

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.pagebean.PageBean;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}")

public class DemoScrollPaneReference
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    String m_bgpaintVertical = "";
    public String getBgpaintVertical() { return m_bgpaintVertical; }
    public void setBgpaintVertical(String value) { this.m_bgpaintVertical = value; }

    String m_bgpaintHorizontal = "";
    public String getBgpaintHorizontal() { return m_bgpaintHorizontal; }
    public void setBgpaintHorizontal(String value) { this.m_bgpaintHorizontal = value; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    /* Listener to the user of the page bean. */
    public interface IListener
    {
    }
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    private IListener m_listener;
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScrollPaneReference(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
        for (int i=0; i<20; i++)
        {
            int y = i * 100;
            if (i != 0) m_bgpaintVertical += "line(0,"+y+",100,"+y+",1,#000000);";
            m_bgpaintVertical += "write(5,"+(y+5)+","+y+",lefttop);";
            int x = i * 100;
            if (i != 0) m_bgpaintHorizontal += "line("+x+",0,"+x+",100,1,#000000);";
            m_bgpaintHorizontal += "write("+(x+5)+",5,"+x+",lefttop);";
        }
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscrollpanereference.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScrollPaneReference}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Initialization of the bean. Add any parameter that is required within your scenario. */
    public void prepare(IListener listener)
    {
        m_listener = listener;
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Scroll pane navigator

The component SCROLLPANENVIGATOR renders the content of a SCROLLPANE component and allows to smartly navigate within the scroll pane.

Pleas note:

(.) The scroll pane is referenced by attribute REFSCROLLPANEID - pointing to the ID of the SCROLLPANE

(.) The component can be placed "everywhere". In the example the SCROLLPANE is the base item of an OVERLAYAREA and the SCROLLPANENAVIGATOR is arranged on top. But you may place it anywhere else, too.

(.) The component takes over the DOM tree of the original SCROLLPANE and renders it internally. So it actually operated on a cloned DOM tree. The cloning is executed at the beginning and then need to be triggered: whenever the rendering of the content is updated, you also have to trigger the cloning so that the navigator area is kept up to date.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_4" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2}" >
<t:row id="g_54" >
<t:overlayarea id="g_5" height="100%" width="100%" >
<t:overlayareabaseitem id="g_6" >
<t:scrollpane id="SCPA2" border="#c0c0c0" height="100%" padding="20" rowdistance="10" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_58" >
<t:paintarea id="g_2" >
<t:dynamiccontent id="g_3" contentbinding="#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2.dynContent}" />
</t:paintarea>
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:overlayareabaseitem>
<tpbc:moveablearea id="g_55" >
<tpbc:moveableareacontent id="g_9" >
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:scrollpanenavigator id="g_56" height="200" refscrollpaneid="SCPA2" triggercontentclone="#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2.triggerClone}" width="200" />
</t:row>
</tpbc:moveableareacontent>
</tpbc:moveablearea>
</t:overlayarea>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.List;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.LABELNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.PAINTAREAITEMNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.componentnodes.PAINTAREALINEITEMNode;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.DYNAMICCONTENTBinding;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding.ComponentNode;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2}")

public class DemoScrollPaneNavigator2
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    DYNAMICCONTENTBinding m_dynContent = new DYNAMICCONTENTBinding();

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScrollPaneNavigator2(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);       
        renderContent();
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscrollpanenavigator2.xml"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScrollPaneNavigator2}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DYNAMICCONTENTBinding getDynContent() { return m_dynContent; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    private void renderContent()
    {
        List<ComponentNode> l = new ArrayList<ROWDYNAMICCONTENTBinding.ComponentNode>();
        int w = 120;
        int h = 80;
        int d = 100;
        for (int i=0; i<10; i++)
        {
            for (int j=0; j<10; j++)
            {
                PAINTAREAITEMNode pin = new PAINTAREAITEMNode()
                    .setBounds((i*w+(i+1)*d)+";" +
                               (j*h+(j+1)*d)+";" +
                               w + ";" +
                               h)
                    .setBorder("#C0C0C0")
                    .setBackground("#F0F0F0")
                    .setRounding(10);
                LABELNode lab = new LABELNode()
                    .setText(i+"/"+j)
                    .setAlign("center");
                pin.addSubNode(lab);
                l.add(pin);
                if (i > 0)
                {
                    PAINTAREALINEITEMNode lin = new PAINTAREALINEITEMNode()
                        .setBounds(((i)*w+(i)*d)+";" +
                                   (j*h+(j+1)*d+h/2)+";" +
                                   d + ";" +
                                   0)
                        .setArrowto(1);
                    l.add(lin);
                }
            }
        }
        m_dynContent.setContentNodes(l);
    }

    
}

Split Pane - Extended Functions

Write back Divider Location

Move the divider within the split pane and press "Synchronize" afterwards: the current location of the divider will be transferred back to the server.

By setting attribute WITHWRITEBACKDIVIDERLOCATION you define that user updates to the split pane update the corresponding property on server side.

As usual within the CaptainCasa client changes to the property are queued at client side, waiting for the next roundtrip. By setting FLUSH to true, the changes are immediately published - together with an action event.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSplitPaneSet} }" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:pane id="g_3" padding="20" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:label id="g_5" text="Current divider location" width="150" />
<t:field id="g_6" flush="true" text="#{d.DemoSplitPaneSet.dividerLocation}" width="100" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
<t:rowline id="g_7" />
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:splitpane id="g_9" dividerlocation="#{d.DemoSplitPaneSet.dividerLocation}" dividersize="10" flush="true" height="100%" orientation="horizonztal" width="100%" withwritebackdividerlocation="true" >
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_10" background="#FF000080" >
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_12" text="Left split" />
</t:row>
</t:splitpanesplit>
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_13" background="#00FF0080" >
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_15" text="Right split" />
</t:row>
</t:splitpanesplit>
</t:splitpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;

Quick Navigation

By setting attribute ONETOUCHEXPANDABLE to true two icons will be added to the divider between the split pane parts.

The user can quickly collapse/re-open the corresponding part by clicking onto the corresponding icon.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

<t:splitpanesplit id="g_6" background="#ffffff80" />
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_7" >

<t:splitpane id="g_9" dividerlocation="50%" dividersize="15" height="100%" onetouchexpandable="true" orientation="vertical" width="100%" >

Divider Location Settings

This example shows different ways of using the attribute DIVDELOCATION.

By default it is interpreted as a (scaled) pixel or percentage value that is seen "from the left".

(.) 150 ==> 150 from the left
(.) 50% ==> 50% from the left

If you define the value lower than -10000, then the value is interpeted as (scaled) pixel value that is seen "from the right".

(.) -10150 ==> 150 from the right

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSplitPaneTypes}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Different Types of Divider Location" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:label id="g_5" font="size:12" text="&#34;On the left, 150&#34;" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:splitpane id="g_7" dividerlocation="150" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_8" />
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_9" />
</t:splitpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:label id="g_11" font="size:12" text="&#34;In the middle, at 50%&#34;" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_12" >
<t:splitpane id="g_13" dividerlocation="50%" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_14" />
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_15" />
</t:splitpane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:label id="g_17" font="size:12" text="&#34;On the right, 150&#34;" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_18" >
<t:splitpane id="g_19" dividerlocation="-10150" height="100" width="100%" >
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_20" />
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_21" />
</t:splitpane>
</t:row>

Hide split areas (+ divider)

Sometimes you want to completely hide the one of the split areas of a split pane.

To do so there are two attributes:

(.) HIDEFIRSTSPLIT
(.) HIDESECONDSPLIT

By passing boolean values you can control the visibility of both areas.

What's the difference to setting the DIVIDERLOCATION to "0"?
If hiding the areas, then also the divider between the areas is hidden so that the user is not able anymore to open the corresponding area by moving the divider.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSplitPaneHide}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Press one of the checkboxes:" />
<t:coldistance id="g_4" width="10" />
<t:checkbox id="g_5" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoSplitPaneHide.leftHidden}" text="Left split hidden" />
<t:checkbox id="g_6" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoSplitPaneHide.rightHidden}" text="Right split hidden" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_7" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:splitpane id="g_9" border="#00000018" dividerlocation="50%" dividersize="10" height="100%" hidefirstsplit="#{d.DemoSplitPaneHide.leftHidden}" hidesecondsplit="#{d.DemoSplitPaneHide.rightHidden}" orientation="horizontal" width="100%" >
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_10" background="#F0FFF0" >
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_12" align="center" height="100%" text="Left split" valign="middle" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:splitpanesplit>
<t:splitpanesplit id="g_13" background="#F0F0FF" >
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:label id="g_15" align="center" height="100%" text="Right split" valign="middle" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:splitpanesplit>
</t:splitpane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

Tiled Area

The TILEDAREA component arranges page bean instances in so called tiles. The tiles can be moved by the user by dragging them within their title area.

The information about a concrete tile arrangement is persisted.

The counter part of the TILEDAREA component is the binding class TILEDAREABinding on server side. The class provides corresponding methods to add tiles. Each tile is represented by an id, a title and a corresponding page bean object.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowheader id="g_1" >
<t:coldistance id="g_2" width="100%" />
<t:button id="g_3" actionListener="#{d.DemoTiledArea.onClearHomeAddress}" text="Remove Home Address Tile" />
<t:coldistance id="g_4" width="50" />
</t:rowheader>
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_5" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTiledArea}" >
<t:row id="g_6" >
<t:tiledarea id="g_7" objectbinding="#{d.DemoTiledArea.tiledAreaBinding}" persistid="demotiledarea" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.elements.impl.TILEDAREABinding;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoTiledArea}")

public class DemoTiledArea
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    TILEDAREABinding m_tiledAreaBinding = new TILEDAREABinding();
    
    DemoPageBeanAddress m_homeAddress = new DemoPageBeanAddress();
    DemoPageBeanAddress m_businessAddress = new DemoPageBeanAddress();
    DemoPageBeanAddress m_vacationAddress = new DemoPageBeanAddress();

    public DemoTiledArea(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
        m_homeAddress.setStreet1("Home Street 1");
        m_homeAddress.setStreet2("Home Street 2");
        m_businessAddress.setStreet1("Business Street 1");
        m_businessAddress.setStreet2("Business Street 2");
        m_vacationAddress.setStreet1("Vacation Street 1");
        m_vacationAddress.setStreet2("Vacation Street 2");
        // add tiles
        m_tiledAreaBinding.setDragTitleOnly(true);
        m_tiledAreaBinding.addTile("HOME","Home Address",m_homeAddress,"400");
        m_tiledAreaBinding.addTile("BUSINESS","Business Address",m_businessAddress,"100%");
        m_tiledAreaBinding.addTile("VACATION","Vacation Address",m_vacationAddress);
    }

    public TILEDAREABinding getTiledAreaBinding() { return m_tiledAreaBinding; }
    
    public void onClearHomeAddress(ActionEvent event)
    {
        final String persistId = m_tiledAreaBinding.getPersistid();
        m_tiledAreaBinding.clearTiles();
        m_tiledAreaBinding.addTile("BUSINESS","Business Address",m_businessAddress,"100%");
        m_tiledAreaBinding.addTile("VACATION","Vacation Address",m_vacationAddress);
    }

}

Transfer of actual Size

Pixel size

The component SIZETRANSFER can be arranged inside a PANE. With every roundtrip it reports to the server the current size of its surrounding pane.

You may optionally set the FLUSH attribute to "true". In this case the size will be transferred if it changes. When flush is defined to be "true", then (and only then) also a corresponding actionListener will be called on server side.
There is a certain delay for sending over changes of the screen size, so that there is not too much traffic generated if the user is resizing the screen.

In case of client-scaling (e.g. client rendering scaled to "125%") the size is "down-scaled" accordingly automatically before being sent to the server side. So on server side you will always receive (scaled) pixel values.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:pane id="g_3" background="#00000030" height="100%" padding="20" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" width="100%" >
<t:sizetransfer id="g_4" actionListener="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.onSizeTransferAction}" flush="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.flush}" flushtimer="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.flushDuration}" sizevalue="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.size}" />
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" cutwidth="true" text="The size of the dark area will be transferred" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:coldistance id="g_8" width="100%" />
<t:checkbox id="g_9" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.flush}" text="Flush size updates &#34;immediately&#34;" width="250" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_10" >
<t:coldistance id="g_11" width="100%" />
<t:formattedfield id="g_12" flush="true" flushtimer="800" labeltext="Flush duration" placeholder="default is 250" unittext="ms" value="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.flushDuration}" width="250" />
</t:row>
<t:rowdistance id="g_13" height="10" />
<t:row id="g_14" >
<t:button id="g_15" actionListener="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.onButtonAction}" text="Synchronize" width="100+" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:field id="g_17" labeltext="Size value" text="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer.size}" width="200" />
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.defaultscreens.Statusbar;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoSizeTransfer}")

public class DemoSizeTransfer
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    Integer m_flushDuration = null;
    public Integer getFlushDuration() { return m_flushDuration; }
    public void setFlushDuration(Integer value) { this.m_flushDuration = value; }

    boolean m_flush = false;
    protected String m_size;
    
    public DemoSizeTransfer(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
        initRefComponent("sizetransfer"); 
    }

    public String getSize() { return m_size; }
    public void setSize(String value) { m_size = value; }

    public boolean getFlush() { return m_flush; }
    public void setFlush(boolean value) { this.m_flush = value; }

    public void onButtonAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("BUTTON: The size of the gray client area is: " + m_size);
    }
    
    public void onSizeTransferAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("SIZETRANSFER: The size of the gray client area is: " + m_size);
    }
}

Category size

This SIZETRANSFER component can be used to not directly transfer pixel sizes, but to transfer size categories.

To do so you need to define the attributes HORIZONTALCATEGORIES and/or VERTICALCATEGORIES.

Each attribute is a string in which you define the name of each category and the corresponding pixel size.

Example: if you define HORIZONTALCATEGORIES to be "narrow:400;normal:800;wide:1200" then the width that is transferred is "narrow" if the screen is up to 400 pixels wide, it is "normal" if the screen is up to 800 pixels wide and it is "wide" for the rest. The highest category is always used if no other, higher category is defined.

The advantage of using the categories is: the client only transfers change of its size to the server, if the changes are relevant on category level. If the corresponding PANE's size changes, but still in the range of its current categories, then no server update is initiated.

Please note: you still need to define FLUSH to be true, if changes should be communicated to the server directly! Otherwise changes will wait for the next synch (e.g. due to a button being pressed).

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSizeTransferCategory}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:pane id="g_3" background="#00000030" height="100%" padding="20" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" width="100%" >
<t:sizetransfer id="g_4" actionListener="#{d.DemoSizeTransferCategory.onSizeTransferAction}" flush="true" horizontalcategories="narrow:400;normal:800;wide:1200" sizevalue="#{d.DemoSizeTransferCategory.size}" verticalcategories="all:10000" />
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:label id="g_6" text="The size of the dark area will be transferred" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:button id="g_8" actionListener="#{d.DemoSizeTransferCategory.onButtonAction}" text="Call Server" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
<t:pageaddons id="g_pa"/>
</t:layoutdefinition>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoSizeTransferCategory}")

public class DemoSizeTransferCategory
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    boolean m_flush = false;
    protected String m_size;
    
    public DemoSizeTransferCategory(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
        initRefComponent("sizetransfer"); 
    }

    public String getSize() { return m_size; }
    public void setSize(String value) { m_size = value; }

    public boolean getFlush() { return m_flush; }
    public void setFlush(boolean value) { this.m_flush = value; }

    public void onButtonAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("BUTTON: The size of the gray client area is: " + m_size);
    }
    
    public void onSizeTransferAction(ActionEvent event)
    {
        Statusbar.outputSuccess("SIZETRANSFER: The size of the gray client area is: " + m_size);
    }
}

Focus Observation

Move the focus into one of the fields. The corresponding area will be highlighted - controlled by a roundtrip to the server.

When setting PANE-FOCUSSENSITIVE to true, then the PANE observes, if the focus is placed inside its content. If so, then a corresponding event is sent to server side (BaseActionEventAreaFocusGained).

Please note: the event is only passed if the user is focussing a component within the PANE "from outside". When the focus is moved within the PANE there is no event triggered.

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.jsfserver.defaultscreens.Statusbar;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoFocusSensitive}")

public class DemoFocusSensitive
    extends PageBean
    implements Serializable
{
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
    int m_focusedArea = -1;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoFocusSensitive(IWorkpageDispatcher dispatcher)
    {
        super(dispatcher);
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demofocussensitive.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoFocusSensitive}"; }
    
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public String getLeftAreaColor() { return m_focusedArea == 0 ? "#FFC0C0" : null; }
    public String getCenterAreaColor() { return m_focusedArea == 1 ? "#FFC0C0" : null; }
    public String getRightAreaColor() { return m_focusedArea == 2 ? "#FFC0C0" : null; }

    public void onLeftAction(ActionEvent event) 
    { 
        m_focusedArea = 0; 
    }
    public void onCenterAction(ActionEvent event) 
    { 
        m_focusedArea = 1; 
    }
    public void onRightAction(ActionEvent event) 
    { 
        m_focusedArea = 2; 
    }

    public void onButtonAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        Statusbar.outputMessage("Button was pressed: " + System.currentTimeMillis());
    }


    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Cascade rendered=false

By setting the attribute CASCADERENDEREDFALSE to "true" the PANE component is NOT rendered if all of its contained children are not rendered. The "rendered=false" information is cascaded up to the level of the PANE component.

The left PANE is a normal PANE with some padding and background definition. It is always rendered - also if it does not contain any rendered content.

The right PANE is the same PANE, the only difference: attribute CASCADERENDEREDFALSE is set to "true". As consequence it completely disappears if its content is set to "rendered=false".

The same thing is demonstrated on ROW level: when switching off both label and field, then the left yellow pane is 10 pixels higher than the right yellow pane. Reason: in the PANE definition there is a ROWDISTANCE of 10 pixels. Because of the cascading in the right pane, the row is not rendered anymore. On the left side there is no cascading and the row is rendered with empty content and as consequence the ROWDISTANCE is applied.

This is the XML layout definition:

    // constructors & initialization

    public boolean getLine2Rendered() { return m_line2Rendered; }

    public boolean getFieldRendered() { return m_fieldRendered; }

    public boolean getLabelRendered() { return m_labelRendered; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    
}

Shift Container

You can slide the content part of the container by dragging and dropping it with the mouse - or by pressing the corresponding buttons on the left/right side.

The page that is currently shown is passed by the attribute VALUE. The attribute value is passed in both directions, you can both set the page index to be opened via your server side logic - and you get notified about the user changing the currently opened page.

Please note: as usual the page index is only passed immediately from the client to the server side processing if attribute FLUSH is set to "true".

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;
import org.eclnt.workplace.WorkpageDispatchedPageBean;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoShiftContainer}")

public class DemoShiftContainer
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    String m_orientation = "horizontal";
    public String getOrientation() { return m_orientation; }
    public void setOrientation(String value) { this.m_orientation = value; }

    int m_selectedPage = 0;
    public int getSelectedPage() { return m_selectedPage; }
    public void setSelectedPage(int value) { this.m_selectedPage = value; }

    public DemoShiftContainer(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoshiftcontainer.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoShiftContainer}"; }
}

Hideable Container

Default usage

Sometimes you want to hide components on client side - but without removing them on the client side.

In this case you may e.g. think about setting the size of the corresponding e.g. pane (0,0), so that it is not visible anymore. But: with setting the size the components are still part of the client component tree - and need to be processed by the client side user interface management.

The HIDEABLE component removes the node below the component itself from the UI management (this means it is taken out of the client side component tree) when its HIDDEN attribute is set to "true". And it re-arranges the component into the component tree when HIDDEN is set to "false".

Please pay attention: you must only add ONE component below the HIDEABLE component! You must not add two or more components!

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoHideable}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:button id="g_3" actionListener="#{d.DemoHideable.onHideAction}" text="Hide/Show area below" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:hideable id="g_5" hidden="#{d.DemoHideable.hidden}" width="100%" >
<t:pane id="g_6" border="#c0c0c0" padding="10" >
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:label id="g_8" stylevariant="ccbig" text="This is the content of the HIDEABLE component" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:label id="g_10" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_11" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_12" text="A field" width="100" />
<t:label id="g_13" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_14" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_15" text="A field" width="100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:label id="g_17" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_18" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_19" text="A field" width="100" />
<t:label id="g_20" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_21" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_22" text="A field" width="100" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_23" >
<t:label id="g_24" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_25" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_26" text="A field" width="100" />
<t:label id="g_27" text="A label" width="100" />
<t:button id="g_28" text="A button" width="100" />
<t:field id="g_29" text="A field" width="100" />
</t:row>

    extends PageBean

{

    public boolean getRowRendered() { return m_rowRendered; }
    public void setRowRendered(boolean value) { this.m_rowRendered = value; }

    public void onHideAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_hidden = !m_hidden;
    }

    boolean m_hidden = false;
    public boolean getHidden() { return m_hidden; }
    public void setHidden(boolean value) { this.m_hidden = value; }

    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demohideable.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoHideable}"; }

}

Type of hiding

If hiding/showing the top area, then the contained BROWSER component always restarts with the URL that is defined behind. Some inner navigation that you might have done is lost.

If hiding/showing the bottom area, then the contained BROWSER component is opened exactly at the state that it had before hiding. Some inner navigation that you might have done is kept.

By default the client side components are removed from the client side component tree when hiding the area.

But you can fine-control this behavior:

By setting attribute TYPEOFHIDING to "resize" (instead of default "remove") the content of the HIDEABLE component is kept as it is, and is removed to widht 0 and height 0. By hiding the content this way, the client state of the content is kept.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoHideableType}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:rowheader id="g_2" coldistance="5" >
<t:checkbox id="g_3" background="#C0FFC0" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoHideableType.hideTop}" text="Top area hidden" />
<t:checkbox id="g_4" background="#C0C0FF" flush="true" selected="#{d.DemoHideableType.hideBottom}" text="Bottom area hidden" />
</t:rowheader>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:hideable id="g_6" height="100%" hidden="#{d.DemoHideableType.hideTop}" width="100%" >

<t:row id="g_8" >

</t:row>

<t:browser id="g_11" height="100%" url="http://www.captaincasa.com" width="100%" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:hideable>
</t:row>

Scale Pane

Scale explicitly set

The SCALEPANE allows to scale its content.

You may position any container into a SCALEPANE instance.
Please pay attention: the SCALEPANE must only hold exactly one container (which itself can contain any content of course!).

By setting WITHUSERSCALING to "true" you can allow to the scale the pane on his/her own (ctrl-mouse-wheel, ctrl-+/-/0 shortcuts).

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_1" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScalePane}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:row id="g_2" >
<t:label id="g_3" text="Scale" width="100" />
<t:slider id="g_4" actionListener="#{d.DemoScalePane.onSliderScaleAction}" flush="true" majortickspacing="50" maxvalue="200" minortickspacing="10" minvalue="50" value="#{d.DemoScalePane.sliderScale}" width="200" snaptoticks="true" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:foldablepane id="g_6" enabled="false" height="100%" text="The content of this area is scaled" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_7" >
<t:scalepane id="g_8" flush="true" height="100%" scale="#{d.DemoScalePane.scale}" width="100%" withuserscaling="true" >
<t:pane id="g_9" border="#00000030" padding="10" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >

</t:row>

This is the Java code:

package workplace;

import java.io.Serializable;
import java.math.BigDecimal;

import javax.faces.event.ActionEvent;

import org.eclnt.editor.annotations.CCGenClass;
import org.eclnt.workplace.IWorkpageDispatcher;

@CCGenClass (expressionBase="#{d.DemoScalePane}")

public class DemoScalePane
    extends PageBean 
    implements Serializable
{
    public void onSliderScaleAction(ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_scale = new BigDecimal(m_sliderScale).divide(new BigDecimal(100));
    }

    int m_sliderScale = 100;
    public int getSliderScale() { return m_sliderScale; }
    public void setSliderScale(int value) { this.m_sliderScale = value; }

    BigDecimal m_scale = new BigDecimal(1);
    public BigDecimal getScale() { return m_scale; }
    public void setScale(BigDecimal value) 
    { 
        this.m_scale = value;
        this.m_sliderScale = Math.round(this.m_scale.floatValue() * 100f);
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // inner classes
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Listener to the user of the page bean. */
    public interface IListener
    {
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // members
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    private IListener m_listener;

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // constructors & initialization
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public DemoScalePane(IWorkpageDispatcher workpageDispatcher)
    {
        super(workpageDispatcher);        
    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscalepane.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScalePane}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    /* Initialization of the bean. Add any parameter that is required within your scenario. */
    public void prepare(IListener listener)
    {
        m_listener = listener;
    }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // private usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
}

Scale automatically set

Resize the green part - the content will be automatically scaled to fit inside.

By setting SCALEPANE-AUTOSCALE to "true" the content will be scaled automatically to fit into the available screen space.

Scale image by user

You can zoom the image by...

...on desktop: use ctrl-MouseWheel
...on tablet/phone: use two finger gesture

Take a look into the layout definition. The zooming is done by a general-purpose SCALEPANE into which the actual IMAGE is embedded.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>

<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScaleImage}" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_4" border="#00000030" height="100%" width="100%" >
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:scalepane id="g_6" height="100%" maxscale="20" minscale="0.1" scale="#{d.DemoScaleImage.scale}" width="100%" withuserscaling="true" >
<t:pane id="g_7" >
<t:rowdistance id="g_8" height="100%" />
<t:row id="g_9" >
<t:coldistance id="g_10" width="100%" />

<t:coldistance id="g_12" width="100%" />

Keep center during scaling

If setting SCALEPANE-WITHSCROLLPOSITIONUPDATE to "true" then the SCALEPANE will search for the SCROLLPANE that it is embedded in - and will update the scroll position so that the center of the current view is kept table.

Using this attribute requires the SCALEPANE to be placed inside a SCROLLPANE!

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:beanprocessing id="g_1" beanbinding="#{d.DemoScalePosition}" />
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoScalePosition}" rowdistance="10" >
<t:rowdistance id="g_3" height="50%" />
<t:row id="g_4" >
<t:coldistance id="g_5" width="50%" />
<t:slider id="g_6" actionListener="#{d.DemoScalePosition.onSliderAction}" flush="true" flushtimer="500" majortickspacing="50" maxvalue="400" minortickspacing="10" minvalue="50" value="#{d.DemoScalePosition.sliderScale}" width="400" />
<t:coldistance id="g_7" width="50%" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_8" >
<t:coldistance id="g_9" width="50%" />
<t:overlayarea id="g_10" >
<t:overlayareabaseitem id="g_11" >
<t:scrollpane id="g_12" height="400" touchscrollsupport="true" width="400" >
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:scalepane id="g_14" actionListener="#{d.DemoScalePosition.onScalePaneAction}" flush="true" height="100%" maxscale="10" minscale="0.5" scale="#{d.DemoScalePosition.scale}" width="100%" withscrollpositionupdate="true" withuserscaling="true" >
<t:pane id="g_15" background="#C0C0C0" >
<t:row id="g_16" >
<t:image id="g_17" image="/images/pictures/carpicture.jpg" />
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:scalepane>
</t:row>
</t:scrollpane>
</t:overlayareabaseitem>
<t:overlayareaitem id="g_18" boundsanchor="centermiddle" x="50%" y="50%" zindex="2" >
<t:drawarea id="g_19" drawcommands="line(50%,0,50%,100%,1,#00FF00);line(0,50%,100%,50%,1,#00FF00)" height="20" width="20" />

    }

    public String getPageName() { return "/workplace/demoscaleposition.jsp"; }
    public String getRootExpressionUsedInPage() { return "#{d.DemoScalePosition}"; }

    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------
    // public usage
    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------

    public void onScalePaneAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_sliderScale = Math.round(m_scale * 100);
        m_sliderScale = (m_sliderScale * 10) / 10;
    }

    public void onSliderAction(javax.faces.event.ActionEvent event) 
    {
        m_scale = (float)m_sliderScale / 100f;
    }

    public int getSliderScale() { return m_sliderScale; }
    public void setSliderScale(int value) { this.m_sliderScale = value; }

    public float getScale() { return m_scale; }
    public void setScale(float value) { this.m_scale = value; }
}

Slide Container

Basics

The SLIDECONTAINER is a container around (exactly!) one content component. If the component exceeds the size of the container then the user can slide the content by mouse (desktop) or by finger (touch device).

You may place any content inside the SLIDECONTAINER. In the example a REPEAT component is used to produce quite a lot of colored rectangles.

This is the XML layout definition:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<t:layoutdefinition xmlns:t="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/t" xmlns:tpbc="http://www.CaptainCasa.com/controllibrary/tpbc" >
<t:rowdemobodypane id="g_2" objectbinding="#{d.DemoSlideContainer}" rowdistance="#{ccstylevalue['@defaultrowdistance@']}" >
<t:row id="g_3" >
<t:label id="g_4" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Some colors - horizontal" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_5" >
<t:slidecontainer id="g_6" background="#00000010" border="0" width="100%" >
<t:pane id="g_7" height="100%" padding="10" >
<t:row id="g_8" coldistance="10" >
<t:repeat id="g_9" listbinding="#{d.DemoSlideContainer.colors}" >
<t:pane id="g_10" background=".{color}" border="#c0c0c0" height="50" width="50" />
</t:repeat>
</t:row>
</t:pane>
</t:slidecontainer>
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_11" >
<t:label id="g_12" stylevariant="ccbig" text="Some colors - vertical" />
</t:row>
<t:row id="g_13" >
<t:slidecontainer id="g_14" background="#00000010" border="0" height="100%" orientation="vertical" >
<t:pane id="g_15" padding="10" rowdistance="10" width="100%" >
<t:repeat id="g_16" listbinding="#{d.DemoSlideContainer.colors}" >
<t:row id="g_17" >
<t:pane id="g_18" background=".{color}" border="#c0c0c0" height="50" width="50" />
</t:row>
</t:repeat>
</t:pane>
</t:slidecontainer>
</t:row>
</t:rowdemobodypane>
